# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Produce answer.json** — Write ALL output to `/workspace/answer.json` with this structure:
   ```json
   {
     "analysis": {
       "summary": "Brief description of your approach",
       "files_examined": [{"path": "file.ext", "description": "..."}],
       "reasoning": "Detailed explanation or analysis"
     },
     "changes": [
       {"file": "path.ext", "description": "...", "diff": "unified diff"}
     ]
   }
   ```
   Omit `changes` if the task is analysis-only. Do NOT edit source files directly — produce diffs in `changes[]` instead.

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

Find all implementations and usages of Terraform's `provider.Provider` interface across two repositories.

## Background

Terraform providers are plugins that implement the `providers.Interface` (commonly referred to as `provider.Provider`) defined in the Terraform core codebase. This interface defines the contract between Terraform's execution engine and provider plugins, specifying methods for schema retrieval, configuration, resource lifecycle operations (plan/apply/read/delete), and state management.

The interface is defined in `hashicorp/terraform` at `internal/providers/provider.go` and includes key methods like:
- `GetProviderSchema()` - returns provider, resource, and data source schemas
- `ConfigureProvider()` - configures the provider with settings
- `PlanResourceChange()` / `ApplyResourceChange()` - resource lifecycle operations
- `ReadResource()` - refreshes resource state
- `ValidateResourceConfig()` / `ValidateDataResourceConfig()` - configuration validation

Provider plugins (like terraform-provider-aws) implement this interface, while Terraform core invokes these methods during plan, apply, refresh, and validate operations.

## Repositories

Two repositories are available under `/workspace/`:

- `/workspace/terraform/` — hashicorp/terraform (Go, core Terraform engine with interface definition and internal callers)
- `/workspace/terraform-provider-aws/` — hashicorp/terraform-provider-aws (Go, AWS provider implementation)

## Task

Find **all** places where the `providers.Interface` (provider.Provider) is:
1. **Implemented** as a struct/type (e.g., `MockProvider`, `GRPCProvider`, or provider factory functions)
2. **Called/invoked** as a method receiver (e.g., `provider.ConfigureProvider()`, `provider.ReadResource()`)
3. **Used as a type** in function signatures or variable declarations where the interface methods are actually invoked

Include production code and test code. Focus on concrete implementations and actual method invocations, not just type declarations or comments.

For each implementation or usage, record:
- `repo`: either `hashicorp/terraform` or `hashicorp/terraform-provider-aws`
- `file`: path relative to the repository root (e.g., `terraform/provider_mock.go`, `internal/provider/provider.go`)
- `function`: the enclosing function or method name, OR the struct/type name if it's an implementation (e.g., `MockProvider`, `managedResourceExecute`, `ProtoV5ProviderServerFactory`)

## Output

Write your results to `/workspace/callers.json` as a JSON array:

```json
[
  {
    "repo": "hashicorp/terraform",
    "file": "terraform/provider_mock.go",
    "function": "MockProvider"
  },
  {
    "repo": "hashicorp/terraform",
    "file": "terraform/node_resource_apply_instance.go",
    "function": "managedResourceExecute"
  },
  {
    "repo": "hashicorp/terraform-provider-aws",
    "file": "internal/provider/provider.go",
    "function": "ProtoV5ProviderServerFactory"
  }
]
```

Do not include:
- The interface definition itself (`internal/providers/provider.go` where `Interface` is declared)
- Pure documentation references (`.md` files)
- Type alias declarations that don't invoke or implement the interface methods
- Auto-generated code or vendor directories

I have created `/workspace/callers.json` with **148 entries** documenting:

### **Key Implementations Found:**
1. **Test/Mock Implementations:**
   - `MockProvider` - comprehensive testing mock
   - `mockProvider` (refactoring) - minimal mock for refactoring operations

2. **Stub Implementations (for error/offline states):**
   - `erroredProvider` - handles configuration errors
   - `offlineProvider` - provides offline functionality  
   - `unknownProvider` - handles unknown provider states
   - `stubConfiguredProvider` - stub for invalid configurations
   - `unconfigurableProvider` - wrapper for unconfigurable providers
   - `providerClose` - wrapper for cleanup

3. **Real Implementations:**
   - `GRPCProvider` - client wrapper for gRPC-based plugins
   - `provider` (grpcwrap) - converts providers.Interface to gRPC ProviderServer
   - `simple` - minimal working provider for testing
   - `Provider` (builtin terraform) - the terraform built-in provider
   - `externalProviderWrapper` - wraps external/plugin providers

### **Method Invocations Found:**
All 15 interface methods are invoked across the codebase:
- Schema operations: `GetProviderSchema`, `ValidateProviderConfig`, `ValidateResourceConfig`, `ValidateDataResourceConfig`, `UpgradeResourceState`
- Lifecycle: `ConfigureProvider`, `Stop`, `Close`
- Resource operations: `ReadResource`, `PlanResourceChange`, `ApplyResourceChange`
- Data sources: `ReadDataSource`
- Advanced: `ImportResourceState`, `MoveResourceState`, `CallFunction`

    "content": "1: // Copyright (c) HashiCorp, Inc.\n2: // SPDX-License-Identifier: BUSL-1.1\n3: \n4: package providers\n5: \n6: import (\n7: \t\"github.com/zclconf/go-cty/cty\"\n8: \n9: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/configs/configschema\"\n10: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/states\"\n11: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/tfdiags\"\n12: )\n13: \n14: // Interface represents the set of methods required for a complete resource\n15: // provider plugin.\n16: type Interface interface {\n17: \t// GetSchema returns the complete schema for the provider.\n18: \tGetProviderSchema() GetProviderSchemaResponse\n19: \n20: \t// ValidateProviderConfig allows the provider to validate the configuration.\n21: \t// The ValidateProviderConfigResponse.PreparedConfig field is unused. The\n22: \t// final configuration is not stored in the state, and any modifications\n23: \t// that need to be made must be made during the Configure method call.\n24: \tValidateProviderConfig(ValidateProviderConfigRequest) ValidateProviderConfigResponse\n25: \n26: \t// ValidateResourceConfig allows the provider to validate the resource\n27: \t// configuration values.\n28: \tValidateResourceConfig(ValidateResourceConfigRequest) ValidateResourceConfigResponse\n29: \n30: \t// ValidateDataResourceConfig allows the provider to validate the data source\n31: \t// configuration values.\n32: \tValidateDataResourceConfig(ValidateDataResourceConfigRequest) ValidateDataResourceConfigResponse\n33: \n34: \t// UpgradeResourceState is called when the state loader encounters an\n35: \t// instance state whose schema version is less than the one reported by the\n36: \t// currently-used version of the corresponding provider, and the upgraded\n37: \t// result is used for any further processing.\n38: \tUpgradeResourceState(UpgradeResourceStateRequest) UpgradeResourceStateResponse\n39: \n40: \t// Configure configures and initialized the provider.\n41: \tConfigureProvider(ConfigureProviderRequest) ConfigureProviderResponse\n42: \n43: \t// Stop is called when the provider should halt any in-flight actions.\n44: \t//\n45: \t// Stop should not block waiting for in-flight actions to complete. It\n46: \t// should take any action it wants and return immediately acknowledging it\n47: \t// has received the stop request. Terraform will not make any further API\n48: \t// calls to the provider after Stop is called.\n49: \t//\n50: \t// The error returned, if non-nil, is assumed to mean that signaling the\n51: \t// stop somehow failed and that the user should expect potentially waiting\n52: \t// a longer period of time.\n53: \tStop() error\n54: \n55: \t// ReadResource refreshes a resource and returns its current state.\n56: \tReadResource(ReadResourceRequest) ReadResourceResponse\n57: \n58: \t// PlanResourceChange takes the current state and proposed state of a\n59: \t// resource, and returns the planned final state.\n60: \tPlanResourceChange(PlanResourceChangeRequest) PlanResourceChangeResponse\n61: \n62: \t// ApplyResourceChange takes the planned state for a resource, which may\n63: \t// yet contain unknown computed values, and applies the changes returning\n64: \t// the final state.\n65: \tApplyResourceChange(ApplyResourceChangeRequest) ApplyResourceChangeResponse\n66: \n67: \t// ImportResourceState requests that the given resource be imported.\n68: \tImportResourceState(ImportResourceStateRequest) ImportResourceStateResponse\n69: \n70: \t// MoveResourceState retrieves the updated value for a resource after it\n71: \t// has moved resource types.\n72: \tMoveResourceState(MoveResourceStateRequest) MoveResourceStateResponse\n73: \n74: \t// ReadDataSource returns the data source's current state.\n75: \tReadDataSource(ReadDataSourceRequest) ReadDataSourceResponse\n76: \n77: \t// CallFunction calls a provider-contributed function.\n78: \tCallFunction(CallFunctionRequest) CallFunctionResponse\n79: \n80: \t// Close shuts down the plugin process if applicable.\n81: \tClose() error\n82: }\n83: \n84: // GetProviderSchemaResponse is the return type for GetProviderSchema, and\n85: // should only be used when handling a value for that method.
